When a CEO takes the spoils of royalty and starts acting like a selfish monarch, he’s no longer leading. He’s taking.

世界最佳教练

The World’s Best Coach

 

看着梅根·麦克唐纳 (Meghan McDonald) 指导 Team Rock 的成员，这并不令人惊叹。 大多数情况下，她只是一对一地安静地与需要听取她意见的人交谈。 在几个小时的过程中，梅根将进行数十次这样的对话。 她偶尔会与整个团队交谈，但从不提高声音。 没有人哭泣，没有人被贬低，没有人被欺负。

Watching Meghan McDonald coach the members of Team Rock is hardly awe-inspiring. Mostly, she just talks quietly, one on one, to someone who needs to hear from her. Over the course of a few hours, Meghan will have dozens of conversations like that. She occasionally talks to the entire team, but she never raises her voice. No one cries, no one is belittled, no one is bullied.

几周后，惊人的事情开始发生。 团队成员开始互相指导。 一名 10 岁的新手向最近从全国比赛中归来的老将提出了建议。 梅根离开大楼，训练继续进行。

After just a few weeks, amazing things start to happen. The members of the team start coaching each other. A ten-year-old novice offers a pointer to a veteran recently back from the national competition. Meghan leaves the building, and practice continues.

体育类比很少对我有用。 它们太不切实际，对现实世界来说太雄性激素了。 然而，梅根不仅仅是一名教练。 她是一个了解真正领导力的人，她明白创建一个部落意味着什么。

Sports analogies rarely work for me. They’re too unrealistic, too testosterone filled for the real world. Meghan, however, isn’t just a coach. She’s someone who understands authentic leadership, and she realizes what it means to create a tribe.

她不会像其他人那样领导。 这很好，因为没有正确的技术、行之有效的策略、正确的方法和错误的方法。 决定领导而不是管理是关键的选择。

She doesn’t lead the way other people lead. And that’s fine, because there isn’t a right technique, a proven tactic, a right way and a wrong way. Deciding to lead, not manage, is the critical choice.

梅根联系和启发。 她管不了。

Meghan connects and inspires. She doesn’t manage.

更紧

Tighter

 

领导者可以关注的第一件事是收紧部落的行为。

The first thing a leader can focus on is the act of tightening the tribe.

扩大部落，吸引更多成员，传播信息是很有诱惑力的。 然而，当与更紧密的部落的影响并列时，这就显得苍白无力了。 一个交流更快、更敏捷、更情绪化的部落是一个繁荣的部落。

It’s tempting to make the tribe bigger, to get more members, to spread the word. This pales, however, when juxtaposed with the effects of a tighter tribe. A tribe that communicates more quickly, with alacrity and emotion, is a tribe that thrives.

一个更紧密的部落更有可能听取其领袖的意见，也更有可能在部落成员之间协调行动和想法。

A tighter tribe is one that is more likely to hear its leader, and more likely still to coordinate action and ideas across the members of the tribe.

Apple 的史蒂夫·乔布斯 (Steve Jobs) 以各种方式收紧了 Apple 狂热者部落。 通过开发大量新产品并在网上发布，他让 Apple 狂热者“收听”新产品成为一种习惯。 在新产品发布后的几个小时内，这个消息就传遍了数百万甚至数千万用户——所有这些都是通过电子方式，全部通过网络实现的。 与此同时，乔布斯对新产品保密的痴迷给苹果带来了一个有趣的副作用：在线谣言网站和猜测进一步助长了苹果粉丝之间的对话。 用户将制作想象中的产品原型并分享图片，甚至挖掘晦涩难懂的专利来证明自己的观点。

Steve Jobs at Apple has tightened the tribe of Apple fanatics in a variety of ways. By creating substantial new products and announcing them online, he’s made it a ritual for Apple fanatics to “tune in” to hear what’s new. Within hours of a new product announcement, the word has spread to millions or even tens of millions of users—all electronically, all online. At the same time, Apple has enjoyed an interesting side effect of Jobs’s obsession with secrecy about new products: online rumor sites and speculation further fuel the conversations among Apple fans. Users will prototype imagined products and share pictures and even dig up obscure patents to prove their points.

这种紧缩可以在没有技术的情况下发生，也可以在没有利润动机的情况下发生。 Keith Ferrazzi 领导着一群聪明的名人和意见领袖——从 Meg Ryan 到 Ben Zander——他仅仅通过收紧部落来领导这个无法领导的群体。 他介绍人。 他请他们吃晚饭。 他找到共同感兴趣的领域，然后避开。

This tightening can happen without technology, and it can happen when there is no profit motive. Keith Ferrazzi leads a tribe of smart celebrities and opinion leaders—from Meg Ryan to Ben Zander—and he leads this unleadable group merely by tightening the tribe. He introduces people. He invites them to dinner. He finds areas of common interest and then gets out of the way.

严密的策略和工具

Tactics and Tools for Tightness

 

互联网和社交媒体的爆炸式增长使营销比以往任何时候都容易。

The Internet and the explosion in social media have made it easier than ever to market.

第一种营销，即传播信息并触及未达人群的行为，允许形成各种部落。 像 Meetup.com 和 Craigslist 这样的网站可以让没有联系的人很容易地建立联系。

The first kind of marketing, the act of spreading the word and reaching the unreached, allows tribes of all sorts to form. Sites like Meetup.com and Craigslist make it easy for people who aren’t connected to become connected.

我对第二种营销更感兴趣，即收紧组织并在部落内传播信息的行为。 博客是查看此方法的一种简单方式。 博主有一个免费的、几乎毫不费力的工具，可以定期（每天？每小时？）向想要阅读它们的人发送消息。 通过评论和引用，部落的成员可以互相顶嘴。 快速进行讨论、分享想法、做出决策。

I’m more interested in the second kind of marketing, the act of tightening your organization and spreading the word within the tribe. A blog is an easy way to see this method in action. A blogger has a free, nearly effortless tool to send regular (daily? hourly?) messages to the people who want to read them. And with comments and trackbacks, the members of the tribe can talk back—and to each other. Discussions take place, ideas are shared, decisions are made—quickly.

关于博客传播领导者思想的力量，我可以写一整本书。 一个未发表的诗人，以前注定要抨击这个制度，现在已经出版了（如果他愿意的话）。 如果想法很棒，它们就会传播开来。 这些思想的传播可以吸引一个部落，诗人从无名到领导。

I could write an entire book about the power of a blog to disseminate a leader’s ideas. An unpublished poet, previously doomed to railing against the system, is now published (if he wants to be). If the ideas are great, they’ll spread. The spread of these ideas can attract a tribe, and the poet goes from anonymity to leadership.

博客也可以在现有组织中发挥作用。 我需要一份影印的时事通讯来激励我在 1984 年共事的工程师； 您可以使用博客并以更强大的方式免费接触更多人。

Blogs can work within existing organizations as well. I needed a photocopied newsletter to galvanize the engineers I worked with in 1984; you can use a blog and reach more people, more powerfully and for free.

互联网公司采用了博客背后的最初想法，并将其扩展为一套工具，任何人都可以使用它来收紧部落。

Internet companies have taken the original idea behind blogs and amplified it into a set of tools that anyone can use to tighten a tribe.

借助 Twitter，微小的更新可以到达成千上万等待收到您的消息并跟随您的领导的人。

With Twitter, tiny driplike updates reach the thousands of people who are waiting to hear from you and follow your lead.

Facebook 的发展方向与 Twitter 相反。 它不是强迫您只使用几个字符，而是可以创建大量的图像、文本和连接。 Facebook 展示了一些人所说的社交图谱。 你认识谁，你怎么认识他们，谁认识谁。 它采用了部落的隐秘世界，并用明亮的数字灯光照亮了它。

Facebook goes in the opposite direction of Twitter. Instead of forcing you to use just a few characters, it enables a huge range of images, text, and connections to be created. Facebook surfaces what some are calling the social graph. Who you know, how you know them, who knows whom. It takes the hidden world of tribes and illuminates it with bright digital light.

Basecamp 是第三种形式的在线互动，与 Twitter 和 Facebook 截然不同，因为它非常谨慎，非常适合管理项目和跟踪工作。 通过访问过去存在于私人电子邮件或手写日志中的内容，Basecamp 使整个部落可以轻松地跟踪进度并感受到您正在建立的势头。

Basecamp is a third form of online interaction, very different from Twitter and Facebook in that it’s quite deliberate, perfect for managing projects and tracking work. By accessing the stuff that used to be in private e-mails or handwritten journals, Basecamp makes it easy for the entire tribe to track progress and feel the momentum that you’re building.

网上的任何东西都无法替代领导层的辛勤工作和慷慨解囊。 但是这些工具使领导力更加强大和富有成效，无论您的部落中有谁。

Nothing online is even close to a substitute for the hard work and generosity that comes from leadership. But these tools make leadership more powerful and productive, regardless of who’s in your tribe.

不适

Discomfort

 

领导力是稀缺的，因为很少有人愿意经历领导所需的不适。 这种稀缺性使领导力变得有价值。 如果每个人都试图一直领导，就不会发生太多事情。 正是不适创造了使领导力有价值的杠杆作用。

Leadership is scarce because few people are willing to go through the discomfort required to lead. This scarcity makes leadership valuable. If everyone tries to lead all the time, not much happens. It’s discomfort that creates the leverage that makes leadership worthwhile.

换句话说，如果每个人都能做到，他们就会做到，而且价值不大。

In other words, if everyone could do it, they would, and it wouldn’t be worth much.

在陌生人面前站起来很不舒服。

It’s uncomfortable to stand up in front of strangers.

提出一个可能会失败的想法是不舒服的。

It’s uncomfortable to propose an idea that might fail.

挑战现状是不舒服的。

It’s uncomfortable to challenge the status quo.

抵制定居的冲动是不舒服的。

It’s uncomfortable to resist the urge to settle.

当您发现不适时，您就找到了需要领导者的地方。

When you identify the discomfort, you’ve found the place where a leader is needed.

如果您作为领导者在工作中没有感到不自在，那么几乎可以肯定您没有发挥领导者的潜力。

If you’re not uncomfortable in your work as a leader, it’s almost certain you’re not reaching your potential as a leader.

追随者

Followers

 

当然，部落也需要追随者。 一个组织，任何组织，都需要不仅愿意追随而且渴望 追随 的人。

Of course, a tribe needs followers too. An organization, any organization, needs people who aren’t just willing to follow, but are eager to follow.

不过，我认为认为你最好的部落新兵是盲羊是错误的。 那些除了盲目地按照指示什么都不做的人在两个方面会让你失望。

I think, though, it’s a mistake to believe that your best tribe recruits are blind sheep. Folks who do nothing but mindlessly follow instructions let you down in two ways.

首先，他们不会在部落成员互动时发挥当地领导作用。 他们会非常忙于遵循剧本，以至于他们会犹豫是否要参与使一个紧密的部落成为一个充满活力的组织的互动。 人们的参与不仅仅是为了提醒彼此现状。 相反，当他们想要改进某些东西时，他们会热切地参与进来。 这种微观领导对于组织的健康发展至关重要。

First, they’re not going to do the local leadership required when tribe members interact. They’re going to be so busy following the playbook that they’ll hesitate about engaging in the interactions that make a tight tribe such a vibrant organization. People don’t engage merely to remind one another of the status quo. Instead, they eagerly engage when they want something to improve. This microleadership is essential to the health of your organization.

其次，他们不会很好地为您的部落招募新成员。 那是因为传福音需要领导。 引导某人放弃一种世界观并拥抱你的世界观并不容易，也并不总是让人舒服。 考虑任何充满活力的群体——政治活动家、非营利志愿者或品牌狂热者。 在每一种情况下，都是战壕中的微型领导者和他们的热情追随者发挥了作用，而不是表面上管理团队的老板。

Second, they’re not going to do a very good job of recruiting new members to your tribe. That’s because evangelism requires leadership. Leading someone toward giving up one worldview and embracing yours isn’t easy and it’s not always comfortable. Consider any vibrant group—political activists, nonprofit volunteers, or brand fanatics. In each case, it’s the microleaders in the trenches and their enthusiastic followers who make the difference, not the honcho who is ostensibly running the group.

前倾，后退，无所事事

Leaning In, Backing Off, Doing Nothing

 

群体创造了真空——停滞不前、什么都没有发生的小空间。 想象一下早期的鸡尾酒会，每个人都站在那里，等待发生什么事情。 或者是开张前的市场，到处都是购物者，但所有商店都用木板封起来，没有任何东西可以创造活力或兴奋。 这里没有部落，只有成群结队、一动不动的孤立个体。

Groups create vacuums—small pockets where stasis sets in, where nothing is happening. Imagine a cocktail party in its early stages, where everyone is standing around, waiting for something to happen. Or a marketplace before it opens, filled with shoppers but with all the stores boarded up, with nothing to create energy or excitement. There are no tribes here, only isolated individuals in groups with no motion.

领导者弄清楚如何踏入这些真空并创造动力。 他们努力工作以产生运动——那种可以将一个群体转变为一个部落的运动。

Leaders figure out how to step into those vacuums and create motion. They work hard to generate movement—the sort of movement that can transform a group into a tribe.

学生可以坐在教室里接受老师发出的信息，然后做作业并过关。 或者她可以采取主动和领导。 她可以挑衅和质疑并要求更多。

A student can sit in a classroom and accept what the teacher is sending out, then do the work and get by. Or she can take initiative and lead. She can provoke and question and ask for more.

营销人员可以提供产品、接受订单，然后继续前进。 或者，他可以利用与潜在客户的互动来创造更多的东西，让客户感到惊喜和愉悦，并产生更多的东西，而不仅仅是物有所值的客户。

A marketer can offer a product, take orders, and move on. Or he can use interactions with prospects to create something more, to surprise and delight and generate far more than just a customer who got her money’s worth.

这种俯身的姿势难得可贵。 2008 年春天，我宣布为学生提供带薪暑期实习。 来自世界各地的 130 多名受过良好教育的学生提出了申请。 作为一项实验，我为申请者建立了一个私人 Facebook 群组，并邀请每个人参与。 他们中的六十人立即加入。

This posture of leaning in is rare and valuable. In the spring of 2008, I announced a paid summer internship for students. More than 130 well-educated students from all over the world applied. As an experiment, I set up a private Facebook group for the applicants and invited each one to participate. Sixty of them joined immediately.

当时还没有部落——在线论坛上只有 60 个陌生人。

No tribe existed yet—just sixty strangers in an online forum.

几个小时内，一些人带头发布话题，开始讨论，参与和领导。 他们呼吁同行做出贡献和参与。

Within hours, a few had taken the lead, posting topics, starting discussions, leaning in and leading. They called on their peers to contribute and participate.

剩下的呢？ 他们潜伏了。 他们坐着看着。 他们躲藏起来，害怕不太可能发生的事情。

And the rest? They lurked. They sat and they watched. They were hiding, afraid of something that wasn’t likely to happen.

你会雇用谁？

Whom would you hire?

潜伏者怎么能想象什么都不做会增加他们被选中的机会？ 他们是否希望仅仅通过观看就能遇到有趣的人或发现新事物？

How could the lurkers imagine that doing nothing would increase the chances that they’d be selected? Were they hoping that they’d meet someone interesting or discover something new by just watching?

这个实验是完美的，因为没有外部因素，没有附带讨论，没有特殊情况——只有 60 个人左右，每个人都表现出自然而然的行为。

The experiment was perfect in that there were no externalities, no side discussions, no special cases—just sixty or so people, each demonstrating behavior that came naturally.

并非所有的领导都涉及面对部落。 成功摆脱困境需要同样多的努力。 吉米·威尔斯 (Jimmy Wales) 领导维基百科不是通过煽动，而是通过让其他人填补真空。 我对实习申请过程的领导包括设置舞台和退后一步，而不是一路推动每一步。

Not all leadership involves getting in the face of the tribe. It takes just as much effort to successfully get out of the way. Jimmy Wales leads Wikipedia not by inciting, but by enabling others to fill the vacuum. My leadership of the internship application process involved setting the stage and stepping back, not pushing at every step along the way.

一条永远行不通的道路是最常见的道路：什么都不做。

The one path that never works is the most common one: doing nothing at all.

没有什么是安全的，而且只需要很少的努力。 它涉及很多合理化和一些隐藏。

Nothing at all feels safe and it takes very little effort. It involves a lot of rationalization and a bit of hiding as well.

退缩和什么都不做之间的区别可能看起来很微妙，但事实并非如此。 退缩的领导者是在对部落的力量做出承诺，并警惕适当的时机重新介入。什么都不做的人只是躲起来。

The difference between backing off and doing nothing may appear subtle, but it’s not. A leader who backs off is making a commitment to the power of the tribe, and is alert to the right moment to step back in. Someone who is doing nothing is merely hiding.

领导是一种选择。 这是什么都不做的选择。

Leadership is a choice. It’s the choice to not do nothing.

前倾，后退，但不要什么都不做。

Lean in, back off, but don’t do nothing.

参与不是领导

Participating Isn’t Leading

 

加拿大 20% 的人口现在使用 Facebook。 许多这些用户有一种错误的印象，即加入一个团体在某种程度上很重要。 它没有。 （加拿大人并不是唯一有相同印象的人。）

Twenty percent of the population of Canada now uses Facebook. Many of those users have the false impression that joining a group somehow matters. It doesn’t. (And Canadians aren’t the only ones with the same impression.)

发送你的简历、出现在社交招待会上、在单身酒吧闲逛——这些都是领导部落的愚蠢方式，它们甚至不是被视为有价值成员的有用方式。

Sending in your résumé, showing up at the networking reception, hanging out at the singles bar—these are dumb ways to lead the tribe, and they’re not even useful ways to be seen as a valued member.

出现是不够的。 在 Facebook 上与十、二十或一千人成为朋友可能对你的自我有好处，但它与任何有用的成功衡量标准都没有关系。

Showing up isn’t sufficient. Friending ten or twenty or a thousand people in Facebook might be good for your ego but it has zero to do with any useful measure of success.

案例研究：CrossFit.com 和 Patientsikeme.com

Case Studies: CrossFit.com and Patientslikeme.com

 

CrossFit 是一群有点疯狂（好吧，真的很疯狂）的健身狂热者。 这些人在任何一天都会做这样的例行公事：

CrossFit is a tribe of slightly crazy (okay, really crazy) fitness fanatics. These are people who on any given day will do a routine like this one:

15 个倒立俯卧撑，接着是 1 个引体向上，接着是 13 个倒立俯卧撑，接着是 3 个引体向上，接着是 11 个倒立俯卧撑，接着是 5 个引体向上，接着是 9 个倒立俯卧撑，接着是七个引体向上，接着是七个倒立俯卧撑，接着是九个引体向上，接着是五个倒立俯卧撑，接着是十一个引体向上，接着是三个倒立俯卧撑，接着是十三个拉俯卧撑，然后是一个倒立俯卧撑，然后是十五个引体向上

 

Fifteen handstand push-ups, followed by one pull-up, followed by thirteen handstand push-ups, followed by three pull-ups, followed by eleven handstand push-ups, followed by five pull-ups, followed by nine handstand push-ups, followed by seven pull-ups, followed by seven handstand push-ups, followed by nine pull-ups, followed by five handstand push-ups, followed by eleven pull-ups, followed by three handstand push-ups, followed by thirteen pull-ups, followed by one handstand push-up, followed by fifteen pull-ups

 

他们 将在与世界各地成千上万人的定时比赛中做到这一点。 在我查看他们网站的那天，有超过四百人发布了他们在这项特定锻炼中的时间。

And they’ll do it in a timed competition against thousands of people around the world. On the day I checked their site, more than four hundred people had posted their times on this particular workout.

全国各地都有认证课程，而且总是提前几周或几个月就卖光了。 越来越多的认证培训师队伍正在世界各地开设健身房，每个健身房都在中央网站协调下寻找自己的 CrossFit 部落新成员。

There are certification courses across the country and they are invariably sold out weeks or months in advance. A growing cadre of certified trainers are opening gyms around the world, each gym finding its own new members of the CrossFit tribe, all coordinated by the central Web site.

CrossFit 部落很强大，而且越来越强大。 这主要是 Greg Glassman（也称为 Coach）的工作。 Coach 从零开始建立了 CrossFit 部落，鼓舞人心、哄骗并制定规则。 没有教练，就没有部落。

The CrossFit tribe is strong and getting stronger. And it’s largely the work of Greg Glassman, otherwise known as Coach. Coach has built the CrossFit tribe from scratch, inspiring and cajoling and laying down the rules. No Coach, no tribe.

格拉斯曼天生就懂得如何领导部落。 他每天都将他们推向极限。 他创造了一种环境，在这种环境中，部落不仅 希望 彼此分享新闻、想法和友情，而且能够 做到 。 部落之所以壮大，是因为个人自豪地自我隔离并代表部落大声疾呼，同时招募和欺负新成员。

Glassman innately understands how to lead the tribe. He pushes them to the limit every day. He creates an environment where the tribe not only wants to share news and ideas and camaraderie with one another, but is able to. And the tribe grows because individuals proudly segregate themselves and speak up on behalf of the tribe, simultaneously recruiting and hazing new members.

将此与我通过纽约时报 上的一篇文章发现的网站 patientslikeme.com 进行比较 。

Compare this to patientslikeme.com, a Web site I discovered via an article in the New York Times.

这是一个似乎没有领袖的部落。 有七千多名病人，每个人都分享了他或她的诊断和当前健康状况的所有细节。 从剂量到副作用，该小组正在建立一个不断增长的数据库，其中包含有关帕金森病和其他衰弱性疾病治疗的真实世界数据。 他们在前进的过程中以热情和安慰相互支持。

Here’s a tribe that appears to be leaderless. There are more than seven thousand ill people, each sharing all the details of his or her diagnosis and current health status. From dosages to side effects, the group is building an ever-growing database of real-world data about treatments for Parkinson’s and other debilitating diseases. And they’re supporting one another with enthusiasm and comfort as they go.

没有 Greg Glassman 或 Oprah Winfrey 为他们欢呼。 他们互相鼓励——谁更好，因为没有人比他们更能欣赏他们正在经历的事情。

There is no Greg Glassman or Oprah Winfrey cheering them on. They cheer one another on—and who better, because no one can appreciate what they’re going through more than they can.

但 patientslikeme.com 的创始人仍然是领导者。 他们找到了一个迫切想要交流的部落，并为他们提供了这样做的工具。 他们使部落更加紧密。 这也是领导力。

But the founders of patientslikeme.com are leaders nonetheless. They found a tribe that desperately wanted to communicate, and they gave them the tools to do so. They made the tribe tighter. That’s leadership as well.

前倾或后退，但不是什么都不做。

Leaning in or backing off, but not doing nothing.

三个饥饿的人和一个部落

Three Hungry Men and a Tribe

 

如果有机会，请前往 http://msg150.com。 这个博客着迷地记录了西雅图 16 个街区的每家餐厅。 对于每家餐厅（大多数是亚洲餐厅），它们都包含筷子的长度和幸运饼干的内容等详细信息。

When you get a chance, head over to http://msg150.com. This blog is obsessively chronicling every restaurant in a sixteen-block square of Seattle. For each restaurant (most of them are Asian), they include details like the length of the chopsticks and the contents of the bonus fortune cookie.

 

 

 

这是一个引用：

Here’s a quote:

我很期待这个地方，因为一些亚马逊伙伴对它的评价很高。 这是一个小地方，需要我们在附近的美食广场吃饭（这很棒，因为我喜欢和瘾君子一起出去玩）。 与典型的一样，我订购了典型的票价，菜单项编号 1，Tonkatsu。 它宣传说它包含“猪肉片”，这对我来说是行不通的。 我选择了额外的猪肉。

…这道拉面就像一碗黄油肥猪肉，加上一些面条来增加口感。 我很佩服他们为我服务的勇气。 它应该和一箱 Newports 一起来，因为显然我的健康与他们无关。 肉汤虽然味道鲜美，但却被猪肉的脂肪淹没了。 然而，猪肉非常棒，味道鲜美，煮熟到分崩离析。

 

I was looking forward to this place, cause some Amazon buddies rated it quite highly. It’s a small place, requiring us to eat in the neighboring food court (which is awesome, cause I like hanging out with crack addicts). As is typical I ordered typical fare, menu item number 1, the Tonkatsu. It advertised that it contained “slice of pork,” which just wasn’t going to work for me. I opted for extra pork.

…This ramen is like a bowl of fatty pork in butter with some noodles added for texture. I admire their bravery in serving this to me. It should come with a carton of Newports, for clearly my health is not their concern. The broth, though flavorful, is overwhelmed with the fatness of the pork. However, the pork is fantastic, delicious, and cooked to the point where it falls apart.

 

我不了解你，但我想加入。我想在这些餐厅的每一家都吃一顿饭，我想发表自己的评论，我想加入这个部落。 如果他们要我参与，我会的。 算我一个。

I don’t know about you, but I want in. I want to eat at every one of these restaurants, I want to post my own reviews, I want to join this tribe. If they ask me to pitch in, I will. I’m in.

其他人会嘲笑并继续前进，想知道这种痴迷是怎么回事。 当然，这就是使它成为一个部落的原因。 有局内人也有局外人。

Others will scoff and move on, wondering what the obsession is all about. That’s what makes it a tribe, of course. There are insiders and outsiders.

好奇心

Curiosity

 

原教旨主义者是这样一个人，他在探索一个事实之前会考虑他的宗教是否可以接受这个事实。

A fundamentalist is a person who considers whether a fact is acceptable to his religion before he explores it.

而不是一个好奇的人先探索，然后考虑他是否愿意接受后果。

As opposed to a curious person who explores first and then considers whether or not he wants to accept the ramifications.

一个好奇的人接受他的宗教和新事物之间的紧张关系，与它搏斗并度过它，然后决定是接受还是拒绝它。

A curious person embraces the tension between his religion and something new, wrestles with it and through it, and then decides whether to embrace the new idea or reject it.

好奇 是关键词。 它与收入无关，与教育无关，当然也与有组织的宗教无关。 它与理解的欲望、尝试的欲望、挑战任何有趣的极限的欲望有关。 领导们很好奇，因为他们迫不及待地想知道这个小组接下来要做什么。 部落的变化才是有趣的地方，好奇心驱使着他们。

Curious is the key word. It has nothing to do with income, nothing to do with education, and certainly nothing to do with organized religion. It has to do with a desire to understand, a desire to try, a desire to push whatever envelope is interesting. Leaders are curious because they can’t wait to find out what the group is going to do next. The changes in the tribe are what are interesting, and curiosity drives them.

好奇的人算数。 不是因为他们有很多，而是因为他们是那些与昏迷的人交谈的人。 他们是领导被困在中间的群众的人。 中间的群众已经给自己洗脑，认为什么都不做是安全的，好奇的人无法忍受。

Curious people count. Not because there are a lot of them, but because they’re the ones who talk to people who are in a stupor. They’re the ones who lead the masses in the middle who are stuck. The masses in the middle have brainwashed themselves into thinking it’s safe to do nothing, which the curious can’t abide.

人们很容易低估一个人变得好奇的难度。 七年、十年，甚至十五年的学业，都要求你不要好奇。 一遍又一遍，好奇的人受到惩罚。

It’s easy to underestimate how difficult it is for someone to become curious. For seven, ten, or even fifteen years of school, you are required to not be curious. Over and over and over again, the curious are punished.

我不认为这是说一个神奇的词的问题； 砰 ，然后突然发生了什么事，你很好奇。 这更像是一个五年、十年或十五年的过程，你开始找到自己的声音，最后你开始意识到你能做的最安全的事情是有风险的，而你能做的最冒险的事情就是安全行事。

I don’t think it’s a matter of saying a magic word; boom and then suddenly something happens and you’re curious. It’s more about a five- or ten- or fifteen-year process where you start finding your voice, and finally you begin to realize that the safest thing you can do feels risky and the riskiest thing you can do is play it safe.

一旦被认出，好奇的安静而持久的声音就不会消失。 曾经。 也许正是这种好奇心会引导我们将自己的伟大与直面我们的平庸区分开来。

Once recognized, the quiet yet persistent voice of curiosity doesn’t go away. Ever. And perhaps it’s such curiosity that will lead us to distinguish our own greatness from the mediocrity that stares us in the face.

我们所看到的是，原教旨主义真的与宗教无关，而与观点有关，无论您的宗教信仰是什么。

What we’re seeing is that fundamentalism really has nothing to do with religion and everything to do with an outlook, regardless what your religion is.

多元神话

The Plurality Myth

 

In order to win an election, you need more than half the votes. 理想情况下，超过一半的人口会支持你，但如果你获得超过一半的选民，你就赢了。

In order to win an election, you need more than half the votes. Ideally, more than half of the population will support you, but you win if you get more than half the voters.

为了领导一个部落，没有这样的规则适用。 您需要做的就是激励选择跟随您的人。 其他人可以无视你或不同意你或继续前进。

In order to lead a tribe, no such rule applies. All you need to do is motivate people who choose to follow you. The rest of the population is free to ignore you or disagree with you or move on.

星巴克不向美国大多数人提供咖啡。 纽约市钩针协会只吸引了一小部分遇到它的人。 没关系。 你不需要多数甚至多数。 事实上，在几乎所有情况下，试图领导所有人都不会领导任何人。

Starbucks doesn’t serve coffee to the majority of people in the United States. The New York City Crochet Guild appeals to just a small percentage of the people who encounter it. That’s okay. You don’t need a plurality or even a majority. In fact, in nearly every case, trying to lead everyone results in leading no one in particular.

这引出了一个有趣的想法：你可以选择你将领导的部落。

This leads to an interesting thought: you get to choose the tribe you will lead.

通过你作为领导者的行动，你吸引了一个想要跟随你的部落。 该部落的世界观与您发送的信息相匹配。

Through your actions as a leader, you attract a tribe that wants to follow you. That tribe has a worldview that matches the message you’re sending.

如果你领导着一个专注于通过对抗全球变暖来拯救世界的部落，那么这个部落当然会有一种世界观，其中包括全球变暖是一个问题并且可以通过其行动来解决的想法。 他们带着这一点来到部落，您的领导与他们产生共鸣。

If you are leading a tribe focused on saving the world by fighting global warming, the tribe will, of course, have a worldview that includes the idea that global warming is a problem and that it can be addressed through its actions. They come to the tribe with that in mind and your leadership resonates with them.

另一方面，如果你选择努力说服一个不同的群体，一个有着截然不同世界观的群体，他们很可能会拒绝你。 阿尔·戈尔 (Al Gore) 开始领导他的部落时，他还不知道他们是谁。 他陈述了他的信息，人们找到了他。

If, on the other hand, you choose to work to persuade a different group, one with a very different worldview, they will likely reject you. Al Gore started leading his tribe when he didn’t know who they were. He stated his message and people found him.

最终，人们最容易被引导到他们想去的地方。 虽然这似乎限制了您的创意或影响力，但这是事实。 福克斯新闻并没有说服数百万人成为保守派； 他们只是聚集了部落并将他们带到了他们已经前往的地方。

Ultimately, people are most easily led where they wanted to go all along. While that may seem as if it limits your originality or influence, it’s true. Fox News didn’t persuade millions of people to become conservatives; they just assembled the tribe and led them where they were already headed.

教师实验

The Schoolteacher Experiment

 

想象一下有相似老师的两个教室。 一个有 15 个学生，另一个有 32 个。 哪个群体得到更好的教育？

Imagine two classrooms with similar teachers. One has fifteen students, the other, thirty-two. Which group gets a better education?

在所有其他条件相同的情况下，较小的班级总是会做得更好。 老师有更多时间为每个学生定制课程。 她的学生较少，因此中断也较少。

All other things being equal, the smaller class will always do better. The teacher has more time to spend customizing the lesson to each student. She has fewer students, hence fewer disruptions as well.

现在，翻转实验。 如果 15 名学生不情愿地把这门课程作为毕业的要求，而 32 名学生必须申请被录取并且很高兴能被录取，那会怎样呢？

Now, flip the experiment around. What if the fifteen students are begrudgingly taking the course as a requirement for graduation, while the thirty-two had to apply to be admitted and are excited to be there.

没有比赛。

No contest.

部落越来越自愿。 没有人被迫为您的公司工作或参加您的服务。 人们可以选择听什么音乐和看什么电影。

Tribes are increasingly voluntary. No one is forced to work for your firm or attend your services. People have a choice of which music to listen to and which movies to watch.

所以伟大的领导者不会试图取悦所有人。 伟大的领导者不会为了让部落变得更大而淡化他们的信息。 相反，他们意识到，在一场运动中，一个积极主动、相互联系的部落比一个更大的群体更强大。

So great leaders don’t try to please everyone. Great leaders don’t water down their message in order to make the tribe a bit bigger. Instead, they realize that a motivated, connected tribe in the midst of a movement is far more powerful than a larger group could ever be.

良性循环与专属部落

The Virtuous Cycle Versus the Exclusive Tribe

 

有些企业规模越大，情况就会越好。 一些非营利组织也这样做。 部落越大越好。

Some businesses get better when they get bigger. Some nonprofits do as well. Tribes that work better when they’re bigger get bigger.

例如，当政党占多数时，政党就会兴旺发达。 Facebook 之所以有效，正是因为每个人都在使用它。 你有一台传真机只是因为和你一起工作的每个人都有。

Political parties, for example, thrive when they’re the majority. Facebook works precisely because everyone uses it. You have a fax machine only because everyone you work with does too.

但更大并不总是答案。

But bigger isn’t always the answer.

一些部落越小越好。 更独家。 更难进入。 有些部落之所以兴盛，正是因为它们规模小。 努力让这些部落中的一个变得更大，你可能会毁了整个事情。 “没有人再去那里了； 它太受欢迎了。”

Some tribes do better when they’re smaller. More exclusive. Harder to get into. Some tribes thrive precisely because they’re small. Push to make one of these tribes bigger and you might just ruin the entire thing. “No one goes there anymore; it’s too popular.”

这总是一个选择。 你的选择。

It’s always a choice. Your choice.

大多数人并不那么重要

Most People Don’t Matter So Much

 

大多数人喜欢他们已有的产品，因此营销人员会忽略它们。

Most people like the products they already have, so marketers ignore them.

大多数人努力工作以适应环境，因此其他人不会注意到他们。

Most people work hard to fit in, so others don’t notice them.

大多数人喜欢在以前吃过饭的地方吃饭。

Most people like eating at places where they’ve eaten before.

大多数人认为这本书是个坏主意。

Most people think this book is a bad idea.

大多数人都希望世界保持原样，但更平静。

Most people would like the world to stay just as it is, but calmer.

大多数人都很害怕。

Most people are afraid.

大多数人直到去年才使用谷歌。

Most people didn’t use Google until last year.

大多数人并不好奇。

Most people aren’t curious.

你不是大多数人。

You’re not most people.

您不是大多数营销人员的目标市场，您当然也不是经理。

You’re not the target market for most marketers, and you’re certainly not a manager.

不仅领导者不是大多数人，而且最重要部落的成员也不是大多数人。

Not only aren’t leaders most people, but the members of the most important tribes aren’t most people either.

追求大多数人 将无法发展您的事业或业务或养活部落。 大多数人真的很擅长忽视新趋势、优秀员工或伟大创意。

You’re not going to be able to grow your career or your business or feed the tribe by going after most people. Most people are really good at ignoring new trends or great employees or big ideas.

你可以整天为大多数人担心，但我向你保证，他们不会为你担心。 无论您大喊大叫，他们都听不到您的声音。

You can worry about most people all day, but I promise you that they’re not worried about you. They can’t hear you, regardless of how hard you yell.

当你不像大多数人，当你努力工作以吸引那些不是大多数人的人时，几乎所有你可以获得的成长都存在。

Almost all the growth that’s available to you exists when you aren’t like most people and when you work hard to appeal to folks who aren’t most people.

现状是否毁了你的一天（每一天）？

Does the Status Quo Ruin Your Day (Every Day)?

 

你今天过得怎么样？

How was your day?

您是否坚持事物的本来面目，而不是忙于将事物变成它们可能的样子？

Are you stuck with the way things were, instead of busy turning things into what they could be?

异教徒有一个计划。 他们明白改变现状不仅有利可图，而且很有趣。

Heretics have a plan. They understand that changing the status quo is not only profitable, but fun too.

作为一个异教徒、一个局外人和一个煽动乌合之众的人感觉很可怕。 何必呢？

Being a heretic, an outsider, and a rabble-rouser feels scary. Why bother?

他们在火刑柱上烧死异教徒

They Burn Heretics at the Stake

 

也淹死他们，斥责他们，不理会他们，把他们吊在椽子上。

They also drown them, denounce them, ignore them, and hang them from the rafters.

我应该用过去时。 这些都不再是真的了。 现在，我们邀请异教徒来达沃斯。 异教徒被选入国会。 当他们的公司上市时，异教徒发了大财。 异教徒不仅热爱他们的工作； 他们也有私人飞机。

I should have used the past tense. None of that is true anymore. Now, we invite heretics to Davos. Heretics get elected to Congress. Heretics make a fortune when their companies go public. Heretics not only love their jobs; they get a private jet too.

木桩的形象很难忘记。 它以一种近乎原始的方式触动了我们。 但它也已经过时了。 营销已经确保了这一点。 那些教我们早餐喝可乐或花 800 美元买一个手提包的力量现在正在改变现状。

The image of the stake is hard to forget. It touches us in a way that’s almost primal. But it’s also obsolete. Marketing has made sure of that. The same forces that taught us to drink Coke for breakfast or spend $800 on a handbag are now at work on the status quo.

异教徒太多了，不能在火刑柱上烧死。 所以我们庆祝他们。

Heretics are too numerous to burn at the stake. So we celebrate them.

错误的问题

The Wrong Question

 

我们快到了，但是你们中的一些人很想问我完全错误的问题，这些问题是：

We’re almost there, but some of you are itching to ask me exactly the wrong questions, which are:

“我该怎么做呢？” 或者更糟：

“How do I do this?” Or even worse:

“我怎样才能让我的老板让我这样做？”

“How do I get my boss to let me do this?”

或者说得直白些：

Or to be really blunt:

“有什么无风险的方式可以潜入系统并获得批准进行更改？”

“What’s the risk-free way to insinuate myself into the system so I get approval to make change?”

当然，有一种方法可以在不被烧死的情况下做出改变吗？

Surely, there’s a method of making change without being burned at the stake?

事实证明是有的，但你已经知道它是什么了。 信仰。

It turns out that there is, but you already know what it is. Belief.

没有人会听你的改变想法，明智地摇头说，“当然，去做吧。”

Nobody is going to listen to your idea for change, sagely shake his head, and say, “Sure, go do that.”

没有人任命你为领导者。

No one anoints you as leader.

没有人会看到您的 PowerPoint 演示文稿并递给您一张支票。

Nobody is going to see your PowerPoint presentation and hand you a check.

更改不是通过请求许可进行的。 稍后通过请求宽恕来进行更改。

Change isn’t made by asking permission. Change is made by asking forgiveness, later.

您只需要知道两件事

All You Need to Know Is Two Things

 

您需要知道的第一件事是，个人拥有的权力比历史上以往任何时候都大得多。 一个人可以改变一个行业。 一个人可以宣战。 一个人可以重塑科学、政治或技术。

The first thing you need to know is that individuals have far more power than ever before in history. One person can change an industry. One person can declare war. One person can reinvent science or politics or technology.

您需要知道的第二件事是，唯一阻碍您成为改变事物的人的因素是：缺乏信念。 相信你能做到。 相信这是值得做的。 相信失败不会摧毁你。

The second thing you need to know is that the only thing holding you back from becoming the kind of person who changes things is this: lack of faith. Faith that you can do it. Faith that it’s worth doing. Faith that failure won’t destroy you.

我们的文化努力阻止变化。 长期以来，我们的制度、组织和标准旨在劝阻人们挑战现状。 我们强制执行我们的系统，并称任何疯狂到足以挑战他们的人为异端。 社会通过将异教徒烧死在火刑柱上来执行这些标准，无论是字面上还是比喻上。

Our culture works hard to prevent change. We have long had systems and organizations and standards designed to dissuade people from challenging the status quo. We enforce our systems and call whoever is crazy enough to challenge them a heretic. And society enforces the standards by burning its heretics at the stake, either literally or figuratively.

但是世界已经发生了很大的变化。 到处都是异教徒。 它是如此不对称，以至于燃烧异教徒不再特别有效。 结果，越来越多的人——优秀的人、有使命感的人、有重要想法的人——站出来做出改变。

But the world has changed a lot. There are heretics everywhere you look. It’s so asymmetrical that burning heretics isn’t particularly effective any longer. As a result, more and more people—good people, people on a mission, people with ideas that matter—are stepping forward and making a difference.

几乎每一个系统，无论是政治的、金融的，甚至是宗教的，都变得不对称了。 这个过程颠倒了：规模不等同于力量； 事实上，水垢会造成伤害。 我们在伊拉克战争中看到了这一点，就像我们在汽水过道战争或新宗教的发展中看到的一样多。 在每种情况下，一个人或一个小团体都有能力颠覆现有系统。

Just about every system, whether it’s political, financial, or even religious, has become asymmetrical. The process has turned upside down: scale isn’t the same as power; in fact, scale can hurt. We’ve seen this in the war in Iraq as much as we’ve seen it in the war in the soda aisle or in the growth of new religions. In each case, an individual or a small group has the power to turn an existing system on its head.

现在，大多数时候，我们称异端领袖。

Now, most of the time, we call heretics leaders.

异教徒赢了。 你可以（而且必须）加入他们。

The heretics are winning. You can (and must) join them.

气球工厂和独角兽

The Balloon Factory and the Unicorn

 

我不确定您是否去过气球工厂。 可能不会。

I’m not sure you’ve ever visited a balloon factory. Probably not.

在气球厂工作的人都很胆小。 害怕，甚至。 他们非常关心大头针、针头和豪猪。 他们不喜欢温度的突然变化。 尖锐的物体也是一个问题。

The people who work in the balloon factory are timid. Afraid, even. They’re very concerned about pins, needles, and porcupines. They don’t like sudden changes in temperature. Sharp objects are a problem as well.

如果你合理化一点，气球工厂并不是一个糟糕的工作场所。 工作很稳定，新年前后有点匆忙。 其余时间它安静祥和，并不那么可怕。

The balloon factory isn’t really a bad place to work if you rationalize a bit. It’s steady work, with a bit of a rush around New Year’s. The rest of the time it’s quiet and peaceful and not so scary.

除非独角兽出现。

Except when the unicorns show up.

起初，气球工厂的人让独角兽闭嘴并警告他走开。 这通常有效。 但有时，独角兽会无视他们，随便溜进工厂。

At first, the balloon factory folks shush the unicorn and warn him away. That often works. But sometimes, the unicorn ignores them and wanders into the factory anyway.

那是每个人都在寻找掩护的时候。

That’s when everyone runs for cover.

独角兽完全破坏气球工厂非常容易。 那是因为工厂是围绕着一个单一的理念组织起来的，即柔和、安静稳定的理念。 独角兽改变了这一切。

It’s amazingly easy for a unicorn to completely disrupt a balloon factory. That’s because the factory is organized around a single idea, the idea of soft, quiet stability. The unicorn changes all that.

气球工厂是关于现状的。 领导者改变现状。

The balloon factory is all about the status quo. And leaders change the status quo.

领导很慷慨

Leaders Are Generous

 

在当今充满活力的政治（和电视）环境中，人们很容易相信，要成为领导者，您需要成为一个自大狂，一个被驱动的超级明星，意图自我美化和强化。

In today’s supercharged political (and TV) environment, it’s easy to believe that in order to lead, you need to be an egomaniac, a driven superstar intent on self-glorification and aggrandizement.

事实上，情况几乎总是相反。

In fact, the opposite is nearly always the case.

着手给予的领导者比寻求获得的领导者更有成效。 更令人惊讶的是，领导者的意图很重要。 部落可以嗅出为什么有人要引起他们的注意。 寻找第一名是一种态度，这是一种不付钱的态度。

Leaders who set out to give are more productive than leaders who seek to get. Even more surprising is the fact that the intent of the leader matters. The tribes can sniff out why someone is asking for their attention. Looking out for number one is an attitude, and it’s one that doesn’t pay.

所以我们有坐在隔间里的首席执行官，就像其他人一样。 我们发现成功的宗教领袖不会乘坐私人飞机飞行，也不会在外面安排豪华轿车等候他们。 我们看着 84 岁的前总统吉米卡特为穷人建造房屋。 这些领导者的利益不是金钱上的，也不是基于地位的……相反，他们通过观察部落的繁荣来获得补偿。

So we have CEOs who sit in cubicles, just like everyone else. We find successful religious leaders who don’t fly by private jet or have a limo waiting for them outside. We watch eighty-four-year-old former president Jimmy Carter building houses for the poor. The benefits to these leaders aren’t monetary or based on status…instead, they get their compensation from watching the tribe thrive.

随着领导部落的能力向更多人开放，有趣的是，那些抓住这个机会的人（以及最常成功的人）这样做是因为他们能为部落做些什么，而不是因为部落能做什么可以为他们做。

As the ability to lead a tribe becomes open to more people, it’s interesting to note that those who take that opportunity (and those who succeed most often) are doing it because of what they can do for the tribe, not because of what the tribe can do for them.

不要忘记巨无霸和微波炉

Don’t Forget the Big Mac and the Microwave Oven

 

1967 年，就在匹兹堡郊外，一位名叫吉姆·德利加蒂 (Jim Delligatti) 的三级麦当劳特许经营商打破常规，发明了一种新的三明治。 一年之内，巨无霸出现在世界各地麦当劳餐厅的菜单上。 （他们甚至在印度提供无肉版本。）

In 1967, just outside of Pittsburgh, a third-tier McDonald’s franchisee named Jim Delligatti broke the rules and invented a new sandwich. Within a year, the Big Mac was on the menu of McDonald’s restaurants around the world. (They even serve a meatless version in India.)

吉姆并没有以牺牲其他一切为代价来专注于管理他的特许经营权。 相反，他成为了领导者。 吉姆没有头衔或官方制裁，但他带领整个公司朝着新的方向前进。

Jim wasn’t focused on managing his franchise at the expense of everything else. Instead, he became a leader. Not blessed with a title or official sanction, Jim led the entire corporation in a new direction.

1946 年，雷神公司 (Raytheon Corporation) 的一名低级工程师珀西·斯宾塞 (Percy Spencer) 在试图改进雷达技术时不小心融化了一块巧克力糖块。 非常聪明的珀西意识到他发明了微波炉。 （下一步：微波爆米花。）几十年来，微波炉几乎成为每个美国家庭的必备电器。

In 1946, Percy Spencer, a low-ranking engineer at the Raytheon Corporation, was trying to improve radar technology when he accidentally melted a chocolate candy bar. Being pretty smart, Percy realized that he had invented the microwave oven. (Next step: microwave popcorn.) Within decades, the microwave oven was a must-have appliance in almost every American home.

这两个故事的非凡之处在于它们是多么罕见。 我们一直听说便利贴的发明和其他伪造的故事，正是因为可供选择的东西不多。 很长一段时间，如果你想完成某件事，你必须从高层开始，否则你真的很幸运。 杠杆来自现金和组织承诺。 如果比尔·盖茨、杰克·韦尔奇或林登·约翰逊认为某件事是个好主意，那么它就更有可能完成。

The remarkable thing about these two stories is how rare they are. We keep hearing about the invention of Post-it notes and other apocryphal tales, precisely because there aren’t that many to choose from. For a long time, if you wanted to get something done, you started at the top or you got really lucky. Leverage came from cash and organizational commitment. If Bill Gates or Jack Welch or Lyndon Johnson thought something was a good idea, it was much more likely to get done.

欢迎来到杠杆时代。 自下而上是一种非常糟糕的思考方式，因为没有底部。 在基层变革的时代，金字塔的顶端距离行动所在的地方太远，无法产生太大影响。 它花费的时间太长，而且缺乏影响力。 顶层不再是顶层，因为街道才是活动所在。

Welcome to the age of leverage. Bottom-up is a really bad way to think about it because there is no bottom. In an era of grassroots change, the top of the pyramid is too far away from where the action is to make much of a difference. It takes too long and it lacks impact. The top isn’t the top anymore because the streets are where the action is.

每个人都可以使用的新杠杆意味着现状比以往任何时候都受到更大的威胁，每个员工现在都有责任在其他人之前改变规则。

The new leverage available to everyone means that the status quo is more threatened than ever, and each employee now has the responsibility to change the rules before someone else does.

这不是要通过遵守规则努力达到顶峰， 然后 开始改变世界的道路。 相反，这些创新是领导力的例子，关于一个异教徒，一个有远见的人，他了解可用的影响力，他勇往直前并改变了一切。

This isn’t about working your way up to the top by following the rules and then starting down the path of changing your world. Instead, these innovations are examples of leadership, about one heretic, someone with a vision who understood the leverage available, who went ahead and changed things.

一些行业通过接受现状而做得很好。 不过，名单每天都在变短。 If you ship oil around the world or sell credit cards or want to get elected village supervisor, you can probably coast for a while longer, embracing the old rules. 但不会再长了。 似乎每个工厂都面临压力：每个气球制造商不仅害怕独角兽，而且迫切需要独角兽。

A few industries do fine by embracing the status quo. The list is getting shorter every day, though. If you ship oil around the world or sell credit cards or want to get elected village supervisor, you can probably coast for a while longer, embracing the old rules. But not that much longer. It seems that every factory is under pressure: every balloon maker not only fears the unicorn but desperately needs one.

家乐氏拥有价值数亿美元的谷物工厂。 他们拥有训练有素的销售队伍、数英里的货架空间和大量的广告。 那么，为什么 Bear Naked 能够在他们眼皮子底下建立起重要的业务呢？ 没有昂贵的工厂或庞大的销售队伍，Bear Naked 采用了一种非常简单、非常传统的产品，改变了许多人购买早餐的方式。

Kellogg’s owns hundreds of millions of dollars’ worth of cereal factories. They have a well-trained sales force, miles of shelf space, and tons of advertising. So why was Bear Naked able to build a significant business right under their nose? Without expensive factories or a huge sales force, Bear Naked took a very simple, very traditional product and changed the way many people buy their breakfast.

Bear Naked 并未尝试管理资产组合。 他们没有试图保护工厂（他们没有要保护的工厂）。 相反，他们引领了一条不同的道路，一条基于时尚、变化和影响力的道路。

Bear Naked didn’t try to manage a portfolio of assets. They didn’t try to protect the factory (they didn’t have one to protect). Instead, they led the way down a different path, one based on fashion and change and leverage.

奇怪的是，增长和成功现在与打破旧规则和在一个不敢改变的行业中放松组织的新规则有着千丝万缕的联系。

Odds are that growth and success are now inextricably linked to breaking the old rules and setting your organization’s new rules loose in an industry too afraid to change.

攀岩

Climbing Rocks

 

Chris Sharma 是一个喜欢攀岩的异教徒。

Chris Sharma is a heretic who climbs rocks.

克里斯改变了整个运动的规则，并一路影响了成千上万人对个人成就的看法。

Chris changed the rules of an entire sport and, along the way, influenced the way tens of thousands of people think about personal achievement.

数百年来，攀岩者遵循一个简单的原则：始终一只脚一只手踩在墙上。 如果你用四肢中的两个固定住，你就可以在不冒生命危险的情况下很好地模仿蜘蛛侠。 右左右左，你往上走，风险很小，进步很大。

For hundreds of years, rock climbers followed a simple principle: one foot and one hand on the wall at all times. If you’re anchored with two out of your four limbs, you can do a pretty good Spiderman imitation without risking your life. Right left right left, up you go, little risk, plenty of progress.

克里斯没有粘在墙上，而是跳了起来。

Instead of staying glued to the wall, Chris jumps.

它被称为测功机。 克里斯并没有发明测功机，但他无疑将它推向了任何人都无法预料的地步。 克里斯可以攀登以前被认为不可能的路线。 当他走到死胡同时，他会抬头跳下。 没有腿，没有胳膊。 只是空气。 笔直向上，两英尺或三英尺或四英尺，用两根手指抓住一小块岩石，继续攀登。

It’s called a dyno. Chris didn’t invent the dyno, but he certainly pushed it further than anyone ever expected it could go. Chris can climb routes that were previously deemed impossible. When he gets to a dead end, he looks up and jumps. No legs, no arms. Just air. Straight up, two or three or four feet, grabbing a small clump of rock with two fingers, and continuing his climb.

有一段时间，这是有争议的。 这是不对的。 这是有 风险的。 然后，一点一点，厂里的人都过来了。 他们发现这是解决大量攀岩问题的合理（但令人惊讶）的解决方案。 突然之间，不可能的路线不再是不可能的。

For a while, this was controversial. It wasn’t right. It was risky. And then, bit by bit, the guys in the factory came around. They discovered that it was a reasonable (but surprising) solution to a large number of rock-climbing problems. Suddenly, impossible routes weren’t impossible any longer.

猜测是，因为克里斯符合典型异教徒的刻板印象，所以你不相信。 他是一个孤独的人； 他冒着生命危险，在地中海上空 40 英尺处做着绝对荒谬的事情（并且经常仰面降落在水中）。 很容易看着克里斯说，“我永远做不到。” 你是对的。 你和我永远不会对 5.14a 岩石拱门进行测功。

The guess is, because Chris fits the stereotype of the typical heretic, you’re not convinced. He’s a loner; he’s risking his life and doing absolutely absurd things forty feet over the Mediterranean (and landing on his back in the water on a regular basis). It’s easy to look at Chris and say, “I could never do that.” And you’d be right. You and I will never dyno a 5.14a rock arch.

教训并不是说您需要冒着手指（更不用说您的生命）在岩石上的风险。 教训是，一个有坚定远见的人可以使改变发生，无论是攀岩还是提供服务。

The lesson isn’t that you need to risk your fingers (not to mention your life) on a rock. The lesson is that one person with a persistent vision can make change happen, whether climbing rocks or delivering services.

这是一个简单的思考方式：美国前攀岩冠军 Obe Carrion 以不同寻常的方式赢得了比赛。 Obe 是四个决赛选手之一，每个人都必须沿着陡峭的墙壁攀登一条非常困难的路线。 前三名决赛选手做了同样的事情。 他们进入用绳子围起来的区域，检查路线，然后慢慢开始攀登，一次一个支撑点，一路攀登到山顶。 两个人成功了（一两次失误）； 一个倒下了。

Here’s a simple way to think about it: Obe Carrion, former U.S. rock-climbing champion, won a tournament in an unusual way. Obe was one of four finalists, and each had to climb a very difficult route up a steep wall. The first three finalists did the same thing. They entered the roped-off area, inspected the route, and then slowly began climbing, one hold at a time, working their way up to the top. Two made it (with a slip or two); one fell.

大部原定最后去。 他从隔离区出来，勘察了一下路线，后退二十步，顺着 城墙 跑了上去。 他没有犹豫、插值或对冲他的赌注。 他只是承诺。

Obe was scheduled to go last. He came out of the isolation area, inspected the route, took twenty steps back and he ran up the wall. He didn’t hesitate or interpolate or hedge his bets. He just committed.

事实证明，这是爬墙最简单的方法。 解决问题使问题消失了。

It turns out that this was the easiest way up the wall. Leaning into the problem made the problem go away.

谁来解决？

Who Settles?

 

定居一点都不好玩。 这是一种恶毒的习惯，是将你带向平庸的滑坡。 经理们总是安顿下来。 他们真的没有选择，因为有太多相互竞争的优先事项。

Settling is no fun. It’s a malignant habit, a slippery slope that takes you to mediocrity. Managers settle all the time. They don’t really have a choice because there are too many competing priorities.

异教徒不会安定下来。 他们不擅长那个。 陷入困境、妥协以保持安静的经理们、每天与官僚作风作斗争的经理们——他们才是解决问题的人。 他们还能做什么？

Heretics don’t settle. They’re not good at that. Managers who are stuck, who compromise to keep things quiet, who battle the bureaucracy every day—they’re the ones who settle. What else can they do?

领导的艺术是了解你不能妥协的事情。

The art of leadership is understanding what you can’t compromise on.

恐惧、信仰和宗教

Fear, Faith, and Religion

 

挑战并改变现状的人会做一些相当困难的事情。 他们克服了他们信任的人、他们为之工作的人、他们社区中的人的阻力。 一路上的每一步，停下来接受气球厂工人对最终放弃的感谢，要比坚持并冒着失败的耻辱要容易得多。

People who challenge and then change the status quo do something that’s quite difficult. They overcome the resistance of people they trust, people they work for, people in their community. Every step along the way, it’s far easier to stop and accept the thanks of the balloon factory workers for finally giving up than it is to persist and risk the humiliation of failure.

那么为什么要这样做呢？

So why do it?

信念是领导者工作中未说明的组成部分，我认为信念被低估了。

Faith is the unstated component in the work of a leader and I think faith is underrated.

矛盾的是，宗教被大大高估了。

Paradoxically, religion is vastly overrated.

信念可以追溯到很久以前。 信心带来希望，并克服恐惧。 信仰赋予我们的祖先应对（前科学）世界的奥秘所需的韧性。 信仰是人类与大多数其他物种之间的分界线。 我们相信太阳明天会升起，相信牛顿定律将继续支配球的运动方式，并相信我们在医学院的时间会在 20 年后得到回报，因为社会仍然需要医生。

Faith goes back a long way. Faith leads to hope, and it overcomes fear. Faith gave our ancestors the resilience they needed to deal with the mysteries of the (pre-science) world. Faith is the dividing line between humans and most other species. We have faith that the sun will rise tomorrow, faith that Newton’s laws will continue to govern the way a ball travels, and faith that our time in med school will pay off twenty years from now because society is still going to need doctors.

Chris Sharma 能够在离地面一百英尺的岩面上进行测功机测试，因为他相信它会成功。 如果您观察孩子们学习如何进行测力计，您会发现发展这项技能的秘诀不是锻炼他们的肌肉或学习一些奇特的技术。 这仅仅是关于培养它会起作用的信念。 “仅仅”当然是一个巨大的进步。 这只不过是一些神经元的信念，只是你能做到的知识。 但是没有信念，飞跃永远不会奏效。

Chris Sharma is able to do a dyno on a rock face one hundred feet above ground because he has faith that it’ll work out okay. If you watch kids learning how to dyno, you’ll see that the secret to developing the skill isn’t about building their muscles or learning some exotic technique. It is merely about developing the faith that it’ll work. “Merely,” of course, is a huge step. It’s nothing but a few neurons’ worth of faith, just the knowledge that you can do it. But without faith, the leap never works.

信念对所有创新都至关重要。 没有信仰，成为领导者、表现得像个异端无异于自杀。

Faith is critical to all innovation. Without faith, it’s suicidal to be a leader, to act like a heretic.

另一方面，宗教代表了一套严格的规则，我们的人类同胞已经将这些规则覆盖在我们的信仰之上。 宗教支持现状并鼓励我们适应，而不是脱颖而出。

Religion, on the other hand, represents a strict set of rules that our fellow humans have overlaid on top of our faith. Religion supports the status quo and encourages us to fit in, not to stand out.

我们的生活中有无数的宗教，而不仅仅是琐罗亚斯德教或犹太教等大写字母 R 宗教。 例如，1960 年代的 IBM 信仰包括工作场所礼仪、着装要求，甚至是表达想法的精确方法（在高架投影仪上）。 百老汇的宗教决定了音乐剧的外观和感觉。 有 MBA 的信仰，一直到标准课程和对成功的看法（在贝恩公司的工作）和什么是不稳定的（去啤酒厂工作）。

There are countless religions in our lives, not just the capital-R religions like Zoroastrianism or Judaism. There’s the IBM religion of the 1960s, for example, which included workplace protocols, dress codes, and even a precise method for presenting ideas (on an overhead projector). There’s the religion of Broadway, which determines what a musical is supposed to look and feel like. There’s the religion of the MBA, right down to the standard curriculum and perceptions of what is successful (a job at Bain & Company) and what’s sort of flaky (going to work for a brewery).

当宗教增强信仰时，它会发挥很大的作用

Religion Works Great When It Amplifies Faith

 

这就是人类发明宗教的原因。 这就是为什么我们有精神宗教、文化宗教和集体宗教。 宗教在需要的时候给我们的信仰一点支持，它让你的同龄人很容易鼓励你接受你的信仰。

That’s why human beings invented religion. It’s why we have spiritual religions and cultural religions and corporate religions. Religion gives our faith a little support when it needs it, and it makes it easy for your peers to encourage you to embrace your faith.

最好的宗教是一种咒语，一种微妙但始终如一的提醒，即信仰是好的，而信仰是到达目的地的途径。

Religion at its best is a sort of mantra, a subtle but consistent reminder that belief is okay, and that faith is the way to get where you’re going.

然而，我们需要谈论这个的原因是，宗教往往恰恰相反。 最糟糕的宗教强化了现状，往往以牺​​牲我们的信仰为代价。 他们在伍尔沃斯百货公司有一种信仰，一成不变地坚持使商店变得伟大的原则，阻止他们将其变成一种新的、更好的体验。 当然，这家商店早已不复存在。

The reason we need to talk about this, though, is that often religion does just the opposite. Religion at its worst reinforces the status quo, often at the expense of our faith. They had a religion at Woolworth’s department store, and sticking, without variation, to the principles that made the store great prevented them from turning it into a new, better kind of experience. The store is long gone, of course.

他们在街上的乡村俱乐部也有宗教信仰。 一套难以改变的信念和规则。 结果，整整一代职业女性都不会加入那个俱乐部，而且它很快就会消失并消失。

They have a religion at the country club down the street as well. A set of convictions and rules that is just too hard to change. As a result, an entire generation of professional women won’t join that club, and it’s going to fade and blow away soon.

挑战宗教和人们想知道你是否在挑战他们的信仰

Challenge Religion and People Wonder if You’re Challenging Their Faith

 

就宗教问题进行深思熟虑的对话之所以如此困难，是因为人们感到受到威胁。 不是因为对特定宗教习俗的仪式或非理性的隐含批评，而是因为这感觉像是对他们信仰的批评。

The reason it’s so difficult to have a considered conversation about religion is that people feel threatened. Not by the implied criticism of the rituals or irrationality of a particular religious practice, but because it feels like criticism of their faith.

正如我们所见，信念是让我们的组织团结在一起的基石。 信仰是做人的基石； 我们离不开它。 但宗教与信仰截然不同。 宗教只是一组发明的协议，（目前）要遵守的规则。 异教徒挑战特定的宗教，但他们是基于非常强大的信仰基础来挑战的。 为了领导，你必须挑战你所生活的宗教的现状。

Faith, as we’ve seen, is the cornerstone that keeps our organizations together. Faith is the cornerstone of humanity; we can’t live without it. But religion is very different from faith. Religion is just a set of invented protocols, rules to live by (for now). Heretics challenge a given religion, but do it from a very strong foundation of faith. In order to lead, you must challenge the status quo of the religion you’re living under.

当然，宗教和信仰是相辅相成的。 你可以通过穿公司制服或说出你当前宗教的咒语来提醒自己你的信仰。 您可以通过出现在教堂或公司野餐会上并遵循所信奉的任何宗教的仪式来接受社区的支持。 没有宗教，信仰就更容易动摇。 难怪宗教一直存在。 它增强了信念，没有它我们就无法成功。

Of course, religion and faith go together. You can remind yourself of your faith by wearing the company uniform or uttering the mantra of your current religion. You can embrace the support of the community by showing up at church or at the company picnic and following the rituals of whichever religion is being practiced. Without religion, it’s easier for faith to flag. It’s no wonder that religion has been around forever. It reinforces faith, and we can’t succeed without it.

所以成功的异教徒创造了他们自己的宗教。 Fast Company 杂志是新宗教的新见证。 它汇集了一群新朋友、新支持者和新仪式。 同样的事情也发生在支持异端行为的公司（如 IDEO）、博客甚至硅谷的巴克餐厅、TED 会议或其他领导者喜欢闲逛的地方。 这些宗教的存在只有一个原因——加强我们的信仰。

So successful heretics create their own religions. Fast Company magazine was a new testament for a new religion. It brought together a new group of friends, new supporters, new rituals. The same thing happens at companies that embrace heretical behavior (like IDEO) and at blogs or even at Buck’s restaurant in Silicon Valley or the TED conference or other places where leaders like to hang out. These religions exist for one reason—to reinforce our faith.

你可以故意这样做。 你可以认识到你的想法需要信仰，你可以找到你需要支持你的部落，是的，你可以围绕你的信仰创建一个新的宗教。 史蒂夫·乔布斯 (Steve Jobs) 在苹果公司故意这样做，而菲尔·奈特 (Phil Knight) 因在耐克 (Nike) 这样做而闻名。

You can do this on purpose. You can recognize the need for faith in your idea, you can find the tribe you need to support you, and yes, you can create a new religion around your faith. Steve Jobs did it on purpose at Apple and Phil Knight is famous for doing it at Nike.

在不放弃信仰的情况下转换宗教

Switching Religions Without Giving Up Faith

 

皮尤人民与新闻研究中心最近的一项研究发现，大约三分之一的美国人已经离开了他们长大的宗教信仰。 该研究错误地使用了信仰一词 ， 但实际上，这些人中很少有人失去信仰。 相反，他们所做的是改变他们用来加强这种信念的系统。

A recent study by the Pew Research Center for the People and the Press found that about a third of all Americans have left the religion they grew up with. The study mistakenly uses the word faith, but in fact, few of these people have lost faith. What they’ve done instead is change the system they use for reinforcing that faith.

当你爱上了系统，你就失去了成长的能力。

When you fall in love with the system, you lose the ability to grow.

信念就是你所做的

Faith Is What You Do

 

如果宗教包含您遵循的规则，那么您采取的行动就会证明您的信仰。

If religion comprises rules you follow, faith is demonstrated by the actions you take.

当你无偿领导时，当你牺牲时没有保证，当你因为相信而冒险时，那么你就是在展示你对部落及其使命的信念。

When you lead without compensation, when you sacrifice without guarantees, when you take risks because you believe, then you are demonstrating your faith in the tribe and its mission.

当然很难。 但是领导会告诉你这是值得的。

Of course it’s difficult. But leaders will tell you that it’s worth it.

一个词

A Word for It

 

宗教和信仰经常被混淆。 反对信仰的人被称为无神论者，并受到广泛的辱骂。 但是对于反对特定宗教的人，我们没有通用词。

Religion and faith are often confused. Someone who opposes faith is called an atheist and widely reviled. But we don’t have a common word for someone who opposes a particular religion.

异教徒 将不得不做。

Heretic will have to do.

如果信仰是信仰体系的基础，那么宗教就是门面和美化环境。 很容易陷入企业文化的弱点和随着时间的推移而建立的系统，但它们与最初建立该系统的信念毫无关系。

If faith is the foundation of a belief system, then religion is the façade and the landscaping. It’s easy to get caught up in the foibles of a corporate culture and the systems that have been built over time, but they have nothing at all to do with the faith that built the system in the first place.

改变是由人们做出的，由那些以被称为异教徒为荣的领导人做出的，因为他们的信仰从未受到质疑。

Change is made by people, by leaders who are proud to be called heretics because their faith is never in question.

在 1515 年，特伦特会议写下了关于异教徒的这篇文章：“最后，所有信徒都被命令不得擅自阅读或拥有任何违反这些规则规定或本清单禁令的书籍。 如果任何人阅读或拥有异教徒的书籍或任何作者的著作，这些作者因异端邪说或涉嫌虚假教义而被谴责和禁止，他将立即被驱逐出境。”

In the year 1515, the Council of Trent wrote this about heretics: “Finally, all the faithful are commanded not to presume to read or possess any books contrary to the prescriptions of these rules or the prohibition of this list. And if anyone should read or possess books by heretics or writings by any author condemned and prohibited by reason of heresy or suspicion of false teaching, he incurs immediately the sentence of excommunication.”

男孩，你有麻烦吗？ 最好摆脱这本书。

Boy, are you in trouble. Better get rid of this book.

Over-the-Top Underdog 勇敢

Over-the-Top Underdog Bravery

 

大约十年来，我的装备包里一直放着一枚硬币。 这是我送给我在 Yoyodyne 领导的团队的七十枚硬币中的一枚，这是我创办的公司。 硬币上附有一个小标签，用于庆祝我们的团队和我们的“Over-the-Top Underdog Bravery”。

For about a decade, I’ve carried a coin in my gear bag. It is one of seventy coins I gave to the team I led at Yoyodyne, a company I started. Attached to the coin is a little tag that celebrates our group and our “Over-the-Top Underdog Bravery.”

领导力几乎总是像失败者一样思考和行动。 那是因为领导者努力改变事情，而获胜的人很少这样做。

Leadership almost always involves thinking and acting like the underdog. That’s because leaders work to change things, and the people who are winning rarely do.

我们所做的（以及您所做的）是勇敢的。 这需要勇气。 管理不会，遵守规则谋生则不会。 这可能是艰苦的工作，但感觉很安全。 改变事物——挑战极限，创造一个尚不存在的未来（同时你受到其他所有人的批评）——需要勇气。

What we did was (and what you do is) courageous. It requires bravery. Managing doesn’t, and following the rules to make a living doesn’t. It might be hard work, but it feels safe. Changing things—pushing the envelope and creating a future that doesn’t exist yet (at the same time you’re criticized by everyone else)—requires bravery.

在顶部？ 这很容易。 普通的思考和普通的努力几乎永远不足以产生领导力。 那是因为我们倾向于勉强做足够的事情。 它需要一些非凡的东西，一个不可抗拒的行动号召，以及一个值得为之奋斗的事业，才能让人们真正加入进来。

And over the top? That’s easy. Ordinary thinking and ordinary effort are almost never enough to generate leadership. That’s because our inclination is to do barely enough. It takes something extraordinary, a call to action that is irresistible, and a cause worth fighting for to make people actually join in.

如果你没有超越顶端，你就没有任何机会让事情发生。

If you’re not over the top, you’re not going to have any chance at all of making things happen.

最简单的事

The Easiest Thing

 

最简单的事情就是做出反应。

The easiest thing is to react.

第二个最简单的事情是回应。

The second easiest thing is to respond.

但最难的是开始。

But the hardest thing is to initiate.

正如 Zig Ziglar 所说，反应是您服用错误药物时身体的反应。 反应是政客们一直在做的事情。 反应是直觉和本能的，通常是危险的。 管理人员反应。

Reacting, as Zig Ziglar has said, is what your body does when you take the wrong kind of medicine. Reacting is what politicians do all the time. Reacting is intuitive and instinctive and usually dangerous. Managers react.

响应是一个更好的选择。 您以深思熟虑的行动回应外部刺激。 组织应对竞争威胁。 个人会对同事或机会做出反应。 反应永远比反应好。

Responding is a much better alternative. You respond to external stimuli with thoughtful action. Organizations respond to competitive threats. Individuals respond to colleagues or to opportunities. Response is always better than reaction.

但与主动性相比，两者都显得苍白无力。 启动确实非常困难，而这正是领导者所做的。 他们看到其他人忽略的东西，然后跳上去。 他们引起了其他人必须做出反应的事件。 他们做出改变。

But both pale in comparison to initiative. Initiating is really and truly difficult, and that’s what leaders do. They see something others are ignoring and they jump on it. They cause the events that others have to react to. They make change.

采取跟随

Take the Follow

 

领导力的优点是如此根深蒂固，以至于很自然地说：“我来带头。”

The merits of leadership are so ingrained that it’s natural to say, “I’ll take the lead.”

但有时，采取以下行动可能更有意义。 当你不知道去哪里，当你没有承诺或激情，或者最糟糕的是，当你无法克服你的恐惧时，领导——这种领导比没有领导更糟糕。

Sometimes, though, it may make more sense to take the follow. Leading when you don’t know where to go, when you don’t have the commitment or the passion, or worst of all, when you can’t overcome your fear—that sort of leading is worse than none at all.

承认也许这一次，现在，你不能领导是需要勇气的。 因此，请让开并跟随。

It takes guts to acknowledge that perhaps this time, right now, you can’t lead. So get out of the way and take the follow instead.

发生在你身上的事情和你所做的事情之间的区别

The Difference Between Things That Happen to You and Things You Do

 

在旧模型中，事情发生在你的工作中。 工厂开张，人被雇用。 老板们下达了指示。 你被调动了。 有裁员。 你升职了 工厂关闭。

In the old model, things happened to you at work. Factories opened, people were hired. Bosses gave instructions. You got transferred. There were layoffs. You got promoted. Factories closed.

另一方面，领导者不会有事情发生在他们身上。 他们做事。

Leaders, on the other hand, don’t have things happen to them. They do things.

在抵押贷款危机期间，我在几千名房地产经纪人的年度大会上花了一些时间。 我的发现可能会让你大吃一惊。 小组完全分裂了。

In the middle of the mortgage crisis, I spent some time with a few thousand Realtors at their annual convention. What I discovered might surprise you. The group was completely split.

一些房地产经纪人看到了媒体、贝尔斯登、银行和公众 对 他们以及他们来之不易的职业所做的事情。 他们对长期上涨的房价结束感到愤怒（甚至是痛苦），他们对自己的未来感到害怕。 这些房地产经纪人不知道他们将如何应对所发生的事情。 他们想管理自己的职业生涯，但变化使之变得不可能。

Some of the Realtors saw what the media, Bear Stearns, the banks, and the public were doing to them and to their hard-won careers. They were angry (even bitter) about the end of a long run of increasing housing prices, and they were scared about their futures. These Realtors didn’t know how they were going to cope with what had happened. They wanted to manage their careers, but change was making it impossible.

其他房地产经纪人显然很兴奋。 他们渴望开始工作。 他们将外部世界的变化视为一个机会，一个让他们大幅增加业务的机会。 他们知道当前的问题不会永远持续下去，而且他们明白这些问题会消灭寻找机会的人，让专业人士站稳脚跟。 大约 10% 或 20% 的房地产经纪人打算辞职，而那些打算留下来的领导者意识到这种变化是一件非常好的事情。 就像士兵们意识到是战争造就了将军一样，这些掮客已经准备好并有动力利用变革作为真正对现状造成破坏的机会。

The other Realtors were palpably excited. They were eager to get to work. They saw the change in the outside world as an opportunity, a chance for them to dramatically increase their business. They knew that the current problems wouldn’t last forever, and they understood that the problems would wipe out the opportunity seekers, leaving the professionals standing. Some 10 or 20 percent of the Realtors were going to quit, and the leaders, the ones who were going to stay, realized that this change was a very good thing. The same way soldiers realize that it’s war that makes generals, these brokers were ready and motivated to use change as a chance to really wreak some havoc on the status quo.

渗透性

Permeability

 

也许你为波音公司或孟山都公司或其他一些企业巨头工作。 不过，更有可能的是，您为一家小型组织工作，可能只有几个人那么小。

Perhaps you work for Boeing or Monsanto or some other corporate behemoth. It’s more likely, though, that you work for a small organization, perhaps as small as just a few people.

无论哪种方式，都值得花一点时间提醒自己过去的样子。

Either way, it’s worth taking a minute to remind yourself of how it used to be.

过去是高管有秘书，秘书有秘书。 你给你的老板（而且只有你的老板）发送了一份备忘录，然后等待一周或一个月的回复。 你没有与同事分享一个新想法——信息的方向最好是向下，或者有时向上，然后向下，但绝不是横向的。

It used to be that executives had secretaries who had secretaries. That you sent a memo to your boss (and only your boss) and then waited a week or a month for a response. That you didn’t share a new idea with a coworker—the direction of information was preferably down, or sometimes up, then down, but never sideways.

Art Kleiner 深入研究的经典著作《 异端时代》 讲述了一个又一个企业异端的故事，这些异端最终被降职、解雇、丢脸和不开心。 公司也可能由约瑟夫斯大林经营——他们有不可更改的五年计划、严格控制的通讯渠道以及围绕君主的皇家法庭。 组织过去是被管理的，没有领导者的位置，也没有异端者的用处。

Art Kleiner’s deeply researched classic, The Age of Heretics, tells stories, one after another, of corporate heretics who ended up demoted, fired, disgraced, and unhappy. Corporations might as well have been run by Joseph Stalin—they had unalterable five-year plans, sharply controlled channels of communication, and a royal court surrounding the monarch. Organizations used to be managed, with no place for leaders, no use for heretics.

长大后，我常去我爸爸的办公室。 我还记得公司办公室男厕所旁边的告示：“工厂员工禁止入内”。 技术娴熟、聪明的车床操作员不仅不被允许使用隔壁办公室的男厕所，而且他们也不经常被邀请与老板分享他们所知道的知识。

Growing up, I used to visit my dad’s office. I still remember the sign next to the corporate office men’s room: “No plant workers.” Not only weren’t the skilled and smart lathe operators allowed to use the men’s room in the adjoining office, but they weren’t often invited to share what they knew with their bosses either.

该系统是刚性的。 例如，柯达在制作胶片时确实让工人处于黑暗中，在漆黑的工厂里辛勤工作。 虽然这个过程需要黑暗，但它不需要严格的管理或信息和权力的囤积。 那只是领土带来的。

The system was rigid. Kodak, for example, literally kept its workers in the dark, toiling in a pitch-black factory as they made film. While the process required darkness, it didn’t require rigid management or the hoarding of information and power. That just came with the territory.

这种方法的问题在于它不能很好地应对不断变化的世界。 当信息来自多个方向、多个来源时，它肯定做得不好。 当与你共事的每个人都阅读《 哈佛商业评论》 和麦肯锡的同一项研究时，事情就变得容易了。

The problem with this approach is that it doesn’t respond well to a changing world. And it certainly doesn’t do well when information comes in from many directions, from many sources. When everyone you worked with read the Harvard Business Review and the same study from McKinsey, it was easy.

最高管理层现在需要领导者。 它想要异教徒在改变发生之前创造改变。 最高管理层明白他们需要追随者，他们必须以变革和非凡的主动性来吸引部落。

Top management now wants leaders. It wants heretics who will create change before change happens to them. Top management understands that they need followers, that they have to engage the tribe with change and remarkable initiative.

但普通民众犹豫不决。

But the rank and file hesitates.

我们犹豫不决，因为我们已经看到了之前发生的事情。 我们害怕失败，害怕批评，害怕犯错，害怕被抓住。 我们担心如果我们停止管理并开始领导，我们将失去工作。

We hesitate because we’ve seen what’s happened before. We’re afraid of failure, of criticism, of making a mistake, and of getting caught. We worry that we’ll lose our jobs if we stop managing and start leading.

杠杆时代改变了这一点，但恐惧依然存在。 三十年前发生在乔、鲍勃或苏身上的古老故事被一遍又一遍地讲述着。 我们用它们来激起我们的恐惧，使我们隐藏的欲望合理化。

The age of leverage changes this, but the fear remains. The old stories of what happened to Joe or Bob or Sue thirty years ago are told over and over. We use them to stoke our fear, to rationalize our desire to hide.

快讯：异教徒现在不仅活着讲述它； 他们实际上茁壮成长。 Jerry Shereshewsky 在 Young & Rubicam 是个异教徒，他傲慢的性格与 1970 年代广告公司的保守文化格格不入。 不用担心。 杰里后来在 BMG 成名，然后和我一起在 Yoyodyne，然后在雅虎，现在在一家名为 grandparents.com 的网络初创公司工作。 相当的职业。 如果他闭嘴，他仍然会推销咖啡机。

News flash: The heretics not only live to tell about it now; they actually thrive. Jerry Shereshewsky was a heretic at Young & Rubicam, where his brash nature didn’t sit well with the buttoned-down culture of a 1970s advertising agency. No worries. Jerry went on to make a name for himself at BMG and then with me at Yoyodyne, then at Yahoo, and now at a Web start-up called grandparents.com. Quite a career. If he had kept his mouth shut, he’d still be marketing coffeemakers.

领导先行

Leaders Go First

 

“每个人都会认为这是愚蠢的！”

“Everyone will think it’s stupid!”

“每个人都说这是不可能的。”

“Everyone says it’s impossible.”

你猜怎么了？ 每个人都在气球厂工作，每个人都错了。

Guess what? Everyone works in the balloon factory and everyone is wrong.

现状是持久和抗拒的。 它存在是因为每个人都希望它存在。 每个人都相信他们所拥有的可能比变化带来的风险和恐惧要好。

The status quo is persistent and resistant. It exists because everyone wants it to. Everyone believes that what they’ve got is probably better than the risk and fear that come with change.

发展中世界的每个人都相信事情会像过去一样。 因此，当企业家精神和技术出现在肯尼亚的一个村庄时，每个人都会抵制。

Everyone in the developing world believes that things are going to be the way they were. So when entrepreneurship and technology show up in a village in Kenya, everyone resists.

一家衰落的唱片公司的每个人都认为，唯一的谋生方式是拥有销售 CD 或数字下载的收入流。 因此，当新的商业模式出现时，每个人都会忽视它们，或者更糟的是，会提起诉讼。

Everyone at a fading record company believes that the only way to make a living is to own the income stream from selling CDs or digital downloads. So when new business models present themselves, everyone ignores them, or worse, sues.

微软的每个人都认为，公司是不可战胜的，硅谷那些小菜一碟的搜索引擎和互联网公司不可能构成威胁。 微软首席执行官史蒂夫鲍尔默说：“谷歌不是一家真正的公司。 这是一座纸牌屋。” 他还说，“在 Facebook 中，没有比几十个人在几年内写出的东西更深的技术了。 这是肯定的。”

Everyone at Microsoft believed that the company was invincible and that the piddling search engines and Internet companies in the Valley couldn’t possibly represent a threat. Steve Ballmer, CEO of Microsoft, said, “Google’s not a real company. It’s a house of cards.” He also said, “There can’t be any more deep technology in Facebook than what dozens of people could write in a couple of years. That’s for sure.”

一遍又一遍，每个人都错了——除非你相信创新可以改变事物，异端可以打破规则，卓越的产品和服务可以传播。

Over and over, everyone is wrong—unless you believe that innovation can change things, that heretics can break the rules, and that remarkable products and services spread.

如果您相信这一点，那么您就不是所有人。 那你是对的。

If you believe that, then you’re not everyone. Then you’re right.

看着音乐行业消亡

Watching the Music Business Die

 

这并不是说他们没有预见到它的到来。 这个蓬勃发展、利润丰厚的行业花了将近十年的时间才自我崩溃。 原因其实很简单：

It’s not as if they didn’t see it coming. It took almost a decade for this thriving, hyperprofitable industry to cave in on itself. The reasons are truly simple:

 
     
  1. 音乐行业的高管们没有他们需要的异教徒。 没有人站出来让改变发生。
  2. Music industry executives didn’t have the heretic they needed. No one stood up and made change happen.
    3.  
  3. 他们忘记了拥抱他们的部落。
  4. They forgot to embrace their tribe.
 

看看音乐行业对任何异教徒来说都是一种有益的教育。 它展示了一个相当新的行业中极其聪明的人是如何故意忽视他们周围的世界并躲起来的。 这些经验教训几乎适用于您能想象到的每个行业。

Taking a look at the music business is a useful education for any heretic. It demonstrates how exceedingly intelligent people in a fairly new industry willfully ignored the world around them and hid. Those lessons apply to just about every industry you can imagine.

音乐行业未能理解的第一条规则是，至少在一开始，新事物很少像旧事物那样好。 如果您从一开始就需要替代方案比现状更好，那么您永远不会开始。

The first rule the music business failed to understand is that, at least at first, the new thing is rarely as good as the old thing was. If you need the alternative to be better than the status quo from the very start, you’ll never begin.

很快，新事物就会比旧事物更好。 但如果你等到那个时候，那就太晚了。 随意怀念旧事物，但不要自欺欺人地相信它会永远存在。 它不会。

Soon enough, the new thing will be better than the old thing. But if you wait until then, it’s going to be too late. Feel free to wax nostalgic about the old thing, but don’t fool yourself into believing that it’s going to be here forever. It won’t.

他们错过的第二条规则是，过去的表现并不能保证未来的成功。

The second rule they missed is that past performance is no guarantee of future success.

每个行业都会发生变化，并最终消失。 虽然您昨天可能以某种方式赚了钱，但没有理由相信您明天会成功。

Every single industry changes and, eventually, fades. While you may have made money doing something a certain way yesterday, there’s no reason to believe you’ll succeed at it tomorrow.

音乐行业与婴儿潮一代一起取得了惊人的发展。 从甲壳虫乐队和迪伦开始，音乐行业的高管们不断地赚钱。 青少年购买力的扩大，再加上摇滚乐的诞生、晶体管的发明以及不断变化的社会习俗，意味着一条很长很长的增长曲线。

The music business had a spectacular run alongside the baby boomers. Starting with the Beatles and Dylan, music industry executives kept minting money. The expanded purchasing power of teens, combined with the birth of rock, the invention of the transistor, and changing social mores meant a long, long growth curve.

结果，音乐行业建立了庞大的系统。 他们创建了头重脚轻的组织、专门的超市、亏损领先的旅游行业、极高的利润率、MTV 等等。 这是一个润滑良好的系统，但关键问题是：为什么它值得永远存在？

As a result, the music business built huge systems. They created top-heavy organizations, dedicated superstores, a loss-leader touring industry, extraordinarily high profit margins, MTV, and more. It was a well-greased system, but the key question is: Why did it deserve to last forever?

它没有。 你的也没有。

It didn’t. Yours doesn’t either.

 

 

 

音乐业务围绕五个支柱建立：

The music business was built around five pillars:

 
     
  • 免费广播推广
  • Free radio promotion
    •  
  • 数量有限的竞争音乐标签
  • A limited number of competing music labels
    •  
  • 制作成本高，需要音乐家从唱片公司获得融资
  • The high cost of production, requiring musicians to get financing from labels
    •  
  • 婴儿潮一代的热门热门歌曲 40 强
  • The Top 40 hits–based focus of the baby boomer generation
    •  
  • 高利润、不可复制的媒体（LP）
  • A high-margin, nonreproducible medium (the LP)
 

请注意，这五个支柱中没有一个与部落或领导层有任何关系。

Notice that none of these five pillars has anything to do with tribes or leadership.

在过去的五年中，这五个支柱中的每一个都已倒塌。 结果是，尽管音乐仍然很丰富，但音乐行业却陷入了困境。

One by one, each of these five pillars has crumbled over the past five years. The result is that while there is still plenty of music, the music business is in trouble.

创新：像收音机一样使用数字发行和互联网，但要做得更好。 从事服务/纪念品业务，而不是起诉客户和怀念过去。 为成千上万的音乐家寻找成千上万的部落，带领他们去往他们想去的地方。

The innovation: use digital distribution and the Internet like radio, but do it better. Be in the services/souvenir business, instead of suing customers and yearning for the old days. Find thousands of tribes for thousands of musicians and lead them where they want to go.

改变商业模式的最佳时机是在你还有动力的时候。

The best time to change your business model is while you still have momentum.

对于一个不知名的艺术家来说，从头开始并建立自己的职业生涯并不容易。 对她来说，一次一个地找到粉丝并建立观众群并不容易。 唱片公司或顶级艺术家很容易做到这一点。 所以跳的时间是昨天。 为时已晚。 好吧，今天呢？

It’s not so easy for an unknown artist to start from scratch and build a career self-publishing. Not so easy for her to find fans, one at a time, and build an audience. Very, very easy for a record label or a top artist to do so. So the time to jump was yesterday. Too late. Okay, how about today?

你越早做，你就必须投入越多的资产和动力。

The sooner you do it, the more assets and momentum you have to put to work.

当新商业模式不如旧商业模式“干净”时不要惊慌

Don’t Panic When the New Business Model Isn’t as “Clean” as the Old One

 

放弃制造毛利率为 90% 的 CD 并转而采用音乐会和纪念品、社区和贺卡以及特殊活动以及感觉像噱头的混合模式并不容易。

It’s not easy to give up the idea of manufacturing CDs with a 90 percent gross margin and switch to a blended model of concerts and souvenirs, of communities and greeting cards and special events and what feels like gimmicks.

克服它。 如果您想留在这个行业，这是唯一的选择。 你不会在五年内卖出很多 CD，是吗？

Get over it. It’s the only option if you want to stay in this business. You’re not going to sell a lot of CDs in five years, are you?

如果这里有生意，前几个进来的人会找到； 其余的将失去一切。

If there’s a business here, the first few in will find it; the rest will lose everything.

业界故意不去阅读墙上的文字。

The industry willfully failed to read the writing on the wall.

工业不会意外死亡。 这并不是说你不知道它即将到来。 这并不是说您不知道该给谁打电话（或雇用）。

Industries don’t die by surprise. It’s not as if you didn’t know it was coming. It’s not as if you didn’t know whom to call (or hire).

缺少的是领导力——一个准备好描述未来并建立实现目标所需的联盟的个人（异教徒）。

What was missing was leadership—an individual (a heretic) ready to describe the future and build the coalitions necessary to get there.

这与有一个好主意无关（几乎从来没有）。 伟大的想法就在那里，免费的，在你附近的博客上。 不，这是关于采取主动并使事情发生。

This isn’t about having a great idea (it almost never is). The great ideas are out there, for free, on your neighborhood blog. Nope, this is about taking initiative and making things happen.

最后离开当前唱片业的人不会是最聪明的，也不会是最成功的。 先出去开拓新领域几乎总能获得回报。

The last person to leave the current record business won’t be the smartest, and he won’t be the most successful either. Getting out first and staking out the new territory almost always pays off.

我知道这很难相信，但过去的好日子还没有到来，即使对于音乐行业也是如此。 问题是，当它重新组合时，过去管理它的人不会在附近，因为他们不会受到欢迎。

I know it’s hard to believe, but the good old days are yet to happen, even for the music business. The thing is, the guys who ran it in the old days won’t be around when it regroups, because they won’t be welcome.

遛羊

Sheepwalking

 

我将 “遛羊” 定义为雇用被培养为听话的人，并给他们提供脑死亡的工作和足够的恐惧来让他们遵守规则的结果。

I define sheepwalking as the outcome of hiring people who have been raised to be obedient and giving them brain-dead jobs and enough fear to keep them in line.

您可能遇到过正在遛羊的人。

You’ve probably encountered someone who is sheepwalking.

TSA 筛查员强迫妈妈喝一瓶母乳，因为手册中没有任何其他操作。 一位客户服务代表会愉快地大声朗读公司政策六七遍，但永远不会停下来考虑政策的含义。 一位营销主管购买了价值数百万美元的电视时间，即使她知道这没有用——她这样做是因为她的老板告诉她这样做。

The TSA screener who forces a mom to drink from a bottle of breast milk because any other action is not in the manual. A customer service representative who will happily read aloud a company policy six or seven times but never stop to consider what the policy means. A marketing executive who buys millions of dollars’ worth of TV time even though she knows it’s not working—she does it because her boss told her to.

具有讽刺意味但并不奇怪的是，在我们这个日益依赖新思想、快速变化和创新的时代，走羊的人数实际上在增加。 那是因为我们不能再依赖机器来做脑死亡的事情。

It’s ironic but not surprising that in our age of increased reliance on new ideas, rapid change, and innovation, sheepwalking is actually on the rise. That’s because we can no longer rely on machines to do the brain-dead stuff.

我们已经机械化了我们可以机械化的东西。 剩下的就是降低必须由人类完成的体力劳动的成本。 因此，我们编写手册并竞相寻找最便宜的劳动力。 毫不奇怪，当我们去雇用这种劳动力时，我们会寻找那些已经被训练得像绵羊一样的人。

We’ve mechanized what we could mechanize. What’s left is to cost-reduce the manual labor that must be done by a human. So we write manuals and race to the bottom in our search for the cheapest possible labor. And it’s not surprising that when we go to hire that labor, we search for people who have already been trained to be sheeplike.

训练学生成为绵羊比其他选择容易得多。 应试教学、确保顺从行为以及使用恐惧作为激励因素是让孩子完成学业的最简单、最快的方法。 那么，为什么我们对这么多羊毕业感到惊讶呢？

Training a student to be a sheep is a lot easier than the alternative. Teaching to the test, ensuring compliant behavior, and using fear as a motivator are the easiest and fastest ways to get a kid through school. So why does it surprise us that we graduate so many sheep?

还有研究生院？ 因为风险更高（机会、成本、学费和就业市场），学生们回到了他们被教导的东西：做羊。 受过良好教育的绵羊，当然，但仍然顺从。

And graduate school? Because the stakes are higher (opportunity, cost, tuition, and the job market), students fall back on what they’ve been taught: to be sheep. Well-educated sheep, of course, but compliant nonetheless.

许多组织不遗余力地聘请那些表现出一致性和合规性的人。 然后这些组织给这些人工作，让他们通过恐惧来管理。 这导致走羊（“我可能会被解雇！”）。

And many organizations go out of their way to hire people who color inside the lines, who demonstrate consistency and compliance. And then these organizations give these people jobs where they are managed via fear. Which leads to sheepwalking (“I might get fired!”).

错不在员工身上，至少一开始不是。 当然，痛苦通常由员工和客户共同承担。

The fault doesn’t lie with the employee, at least not at first. And of course, the pain is often borne by both the employee and the customer.

寻求替代方案是否效率较低？ 当您建立一个扁平、开放并尊重员工的组织时会发生什么？ 当您期望很高并信任与您一起工作的人时会发生什么？ 起初，这似乎很疯狂。 开销太大，可预测性太低，噪音太大。 这不是工厂或国王及其宫廷的自上而下模型。 一片混乱。 很容易拒绝。

Is it less efficient to pursue the alternative? What happens when you build an organization that’s flat and open and treats employees with respect? What happens when you expect a lot and trust the people you work with? At first, it seems crazy. There’s too much overhead, too little predictability, and way too much noise. This isn’t the top-down model of the factory, or the king and his court. It’s chaos. It’s easy to reject out of hand.

然后，一遍又一遍，我们看到一些事情发生了。 当你雇用了不起的人并给他们自由时，他们就会做出惊人的事情。 遛羊人和他们的老板看着并摇头，确信这是一个例外，对他们的行业或他们的客户群来说风险太大了。

Then, over and over, we see something happen. When you hire amazing people and give them freedom, they do amazing stuff. And the sheepwalkers and their bosses watch and shake their heads, certain that this is an exception and that it is way too risky for their industry or their customer base.

上个月我参加了一次谷歌会议，我在一个满是（新成立的）谷歌销售代表的房间里呆了一段时间。 我和他们中的一些人谈了一会儿这个行业的现状。 发现他们在遛羊让我很伤心。

I was at a Google conference last month, and I spent some time in a room filled with (pretty newly minted) Google sales reps. I talked to a few of them for a while about the state of the industry. And it broke my heart to discover that they were sheepwalking.

想想我一周后拜访的一家出版公司的接待员。 她在那里，什么也不做。 坐在办公桌前，忙着自己的事，百无聊赖。 她承认前台很慢，她只是坐在那里，读言情小说等待。 她已经这样做了两年。

Consider the receptionist at a publishing company I visited a week later. There she was, doing nothing. Sitting at a desk, minding her own business, bored out of her skull. She acknowledged that the front office is very slow and that she just sits there, reading romance novels and waiting. And she’s been doing it for two years.

或者想一想我昨天遇到的 MBA 学生，她正在一家大型包装商品公司工作，因为他们给了她丰厚的薪水，并承诺给她一个知名品牌。 她将“只呆十年，然后生个孩子，然后离开，开始我自己的演出”。 她会非常擅长在星期日报纸上刊登优惠券，但不是特别擅长解决新问题。

Or consider the MBA student I met yesterday who is taking a job at a major packaged-goods company because they offered her a great salary and promised her a well-known brand. She’s going to stay “for just ten years, then have a baby and leave and start my own gig.” She’ll get really good at running coupons in the Sunday paper, but not particularly good at solving new problems.

真是浪费。

What a waste.

第一步是给问题起个名字。 遛羊。 完毕。

Step one is to give the problem a name. Sheepwalking. Done.

第二步是让那些在这面镜子中看到自己的人意识到你总是可以停下来。 你总是可以仅仅因为其他人已经在这样做，就拒绝走与其他人相同的道路，从而获得你应得的职业。

Step two is for those of you who see yourself in this mirror to realize that you can always stop. You can always claim the career you deserve merely by refusing to walk down the same path as everyone else just because everyone else is already doing it.

不过，最大的一步来自任教或雇用的任何人。 那就是拥抱非绵羊行为，奖励它并珍惜它。 正如我们所见，几乎所有最近出现增长的地方都是好事发生的地方。

The biggest step, though, comes from anyone who teaches or hires. And that’s to embrace nonsheep behavior, to reward it and cherish it. As we’ve seen, just about everywhere there’s been growth lately is where the good stuff happens.
